scope="row" class="infobox-label">Website</th><td class="infobox-data"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.trujilloalto.pr/">www<wbr />.trujilloalto<wbr />.pr</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Trujillo Alto</b> (<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1177148991">.mw-parser-output .IPA-label-small{font-size:85%}.mw-parser-output .references .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .infobox .IPA-label-small,.mw-parser-output .navbox .IPA-label-small{font-size:100%}</style><span class="IPA-label IPA-label-small">Spanish pronunciation:</span> <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="es-Latn-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Spanish" title="Help:IPA/Spanish">&#91;t\xc9\xbeu\xcb\x88xi\xca\x9do<span class="wrap"> </span>\xcb\x88alto&#93;</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto_barrio-pueblo" title="Trujillo Alto barrio-pueblo">town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Municipalities of Puerto Rico">municipality</a> of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> located in the Northern Coastal Plain, on the boundary between the <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">karst</a> zone and <a href="/wiki/Sierra_de_Luquillo" title="Sierra de Luquillo">Sierra de Luquillo</a>, north of <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Gurabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gurabo, Puerto Rico">Gurabo</a>; southeast of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, and west of <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>. Trujillo Alto is part of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan Metropolitan Area">San Juan Metropolitan Area</a>, which includes the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/Bayam%C3%B3n,_Puerto_Rico" title="Bayam\xc3\xb3n, Puerto Rico">Bayam\xc3\xb3n</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cata%C3%B1o,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cata\xc3\xb1o, Puerto Rico">Cata\xc3\xb1o</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toa_Baja,_Puerto_Rico" title="Toa Baja, Puerto Rico">Toa Baja</a>. The city is spread over 6 barrios and <a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto_barrio-pueblo" title="Trujillo Alto barrio-pueblo">Trujillo Alto Pueblo</a> (the downtown area and the administrative center of the city). It is part of the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo_Metropolitan_Statistical_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area">San Juan-Caguas-Guaynabo Metropolitan Statistical Area</a>.\n</p><p>Trujillo Alto was officially founded in 1801, but gained more importance during the 20th century. Due to its proximity to the capital, <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, the city has become a suburb of the metropolitan area, which has sparked its growth during recent years. The population of Trujillo Alto has increased through the last century from 9,576 (1930) to 74,482 (2010). According to the 2010 Census, it is Puerto Rico\'s tenth-most populated municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1953\xe2\x80\x9354, the <a href="/wiki/Carra%C3%ADzo_Dam" title="Carra\xc3\xadzo Dam">Carra\xc3\xadzo</a> <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectric_dam" class="mw-redirect" title="Hydroelectric dam">hydroelectric dam</a> was constructed in Trujillo Alto by the Sumner Sollitt Construction Company of Chicago, under contract by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Water_Resources_Authority" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Water Resources Authority">Puerto Rico Water Resources Authority</a>. The dam forms the <a href="/wiki/Lo%C3%ADza_Lake" title="Lo\xc3\xadza Lake">Lo\xc3\xadza Lake</a>, a reservoir which serves as the main source of the water supply for <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan, Puerto Rico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The region of what is now Trujillo Alto belonged to the <a href="/wiki/Ta%C3%ADno_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Ta\xc3\xadno people">Ta\xc3\xadno</a> region of Cayniab\xc3\xb3n, which stretched from the northeast coast of Puerto Rico into the central region of the island.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The region was led by <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">cacique</a> Canoban\xc3\xa1. Archeological findings have identified two sites within the municipality of Trujillo Alto with archeological significance: Las Cuevas, which was studied by Irving Rouse, and Quebrada Grande.<sup id="cite_ref-historia_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historia-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="Spanish colonization of the Americas">Spanish colonization</a>, families started settling at both sides of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza</a>. During the 17th century, the Spanish crown granted Alonso Pizarro Hermona, from <a href="/wiki/Trujillo,_C%C3%A1ceres" title="Trujillo, C\xc3\xa1ceres">Trujillo</a> in Spain, a vast ranch that covered the region. Residents began using his family name to refer to the location. Eventually, the inhabitants went to the <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Governor of Puerto Rico">Governor</a> and asked for a permit to build a chapel, which was a requisite to officially found a town. Despite some opposition, Trujillo Alto was founded on January 8, 1801, under the name of <b><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Municipio La Santa Cruz de Trujillo</i></span></b>.<sup id="cite_ref-Orgullo_Trujillano_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Orgullo_Trujillano-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The town was settled on a meander of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza</a>. Around 1820, the name <i>Trujillo Alto</i> was used to differentiate the town from that of <i>Trujillo Bajo</i> (which later became known as <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-prfogui_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prfogui-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Trujillo_Alto_marker_on_PR-181.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Trujillo_Alto_marker_on_PR-181.JPG/250px-Trujillo_Alto_marker_on_PR-181.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="196" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Trujillo_Alto_marker_on_PR-181.JPG/375px-Trujillo_Alto_marker_on_PR-181.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Trujillo_Alto_marker_on_PR-181.JPG/500px-Trujillo_Alto_marker_on_PR-181.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1174" data-file-height="919" /></a><figcaption>Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico, marker on PR-181</figcaption></figure>\n<p>In 1826, communication to and from the town improved with the construction of two bridges: one into <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Piedras,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Piedras, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Piedras</a>, and the other into <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande,_Puerto_Rico" title="R\xc3\xado Grande, Puerto Rico">R\xc3\xado Grande</a>. In 1844, Trujillo Alto was composed of only five barrios. A few years later, the first school was built. During that time, its population decreased notably due to an epidemic of <a href="/wiki/Cholera" title="Cholera">cholera</a>.\n</p><p>In 1898, when Puerto Rico was ceded by Spain, it became a territory of the United States. In 1899, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_War" title="United States Department of War">US Department of War</a> conducted its first census of Puerto Rico and found that the population of Trujillo Alto was 5,683.<sup id="cite_ref-OfficeSanger1900_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OfficeSanger1900-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1902, the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Legislative Assembly of Puerto Rico">Legislative Assembly of Puerto Rico</a> approved a law for the consolidation of certain municipalities. As a result, Trujillo Alto was incorporated into the town and municipality of bordering <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>. In 1905 the law was revoked returning Trujillo Alto to its status of municipality again.<sup id="cite_ref-psh_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psh-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1952, along with the <a href="/wiki/Carra%C3%ADzo_Dam" title="Carra\xc3\xadzo Dam">Carra\xc3\xadzo Dam</a> constructed in barrio <a href="/wiki/Carra%C3%ADzo" title="Carra\xc3\xadzo">Carra\xc3\xadzo</a>, a filtration plant was constructed in barrio Cuevas in Trujillo Alto.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The proximity of the city to the capital, <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, sparked significant growth and development in the region and during the 20th century, the population of Trujillo Alto increased dramatically.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> As of 2010, the city is the tenth-most populous city of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. Mayor <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Cruz_Cruz" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Cruz Cruz">Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Cruz Cruz</a>, who has been serving since 2009, has labeled the city as "<i>The New Metropolis</i>".<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Mountain_village_of_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Mountain_village_of_Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/220px-Mountain_village_of_Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Mountain_village_of_Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/330px-Mountain_village_of_Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Mountain_village_of_Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg/440px-Mountain_village_of_Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a><figcaption>Working to restore power to Trujillo Alto, December 24, 2017</figcaption></figure>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Hurricane Maria</a> on September 20, 2017, triggered numerous landslides in Trujillo Alto, with its rain and winds.<sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USGS_Maria_Landslides_map-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The hurricane winds and rain damaged infrastructure and caused almost the entire electrical system of Trujillo Alto to collapse, leaving its nearly 75,000 residents with no electrical power. Also, 90% of the residents lost access to clean, <a href="/wiki/Drinking_water" title="Drinking water">drinking water</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Geography">Geography</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Carraizo_Lake_Dam,_Puerto_Rico.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Carraizo_Lake_Dam%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG/250px-Carraizo_Lake_Dam%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Carraizo_Lake_Dam%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG/375px-Carraizo_Lake_Dam%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Carraizo_Lake_Dam%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG/500px-Carraizo_Lake_Dam%2C_Puerto_Rico.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a><figcaption>The Carra\xc3\xadzo Lake Dam in Trujillo Alto supplies potable water to the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan Metropolitan Area">San Juan Metropolitan Area</a>.</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Trujillo Alto sits on the Northern Coastal Plain region of Puerto Rico. It is bordered by the municipalities of <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">San Juan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gurabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Gurabo, Puerto Rico">Gurabo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Caguas,_Puerto_Rico" title="Caguas, Puerto Rico">Caguas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-psh_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psh-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Trujillo Alto is a small municipality, covering only 21.47 square miles (55.6&#160;km<sup>2</sup>).<sup id="cite_ref-PR_Ency_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PR_Ency-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Trujillo Alto\'s terrain is mostly plain in the north, while the south features small hills. Heights can range from 660 to 1,600 feet (200\xe2\x80\x93500 meters) above sea level.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Water_features">Water features</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Water features"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Trujillo Alto\'s hydrographic system consists mainly of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza</a>, which crosses the municipality.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There are also several creeks in the city: Colorada, Infierno, Limones, Naranjo, Grande, Pastrana, Haya Fr\xc3\xada, and Maracuto.<sup id="cite_ref-prfogui_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prfogui-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Also, Trujillo Alto is the site of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>\'s main <a href="/wiki/Water_reservoir" class="mw-redirect" title="Water reservoir">water reservoir</a>: The <a href="/wiki/Carra%C3%ADzo_Dam" title="Carra\xc3\xadzo Dam">Carra\xc3\xadzo Dam</a>, at the <a href="/wiki/Lo%C3%ADza_Lake" title="Lo\xc3\xadza Lake">Lo\xc3\xadza Lake</a>. Both were built in 1953 by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Aqueducts_and_Sewers_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Aqueducts and Sewers Authority">Puerto Rico Aqueducts and Sewers Authority</a> (PRASA). Although it was originally built to generate hydroelectricity, it is now used solely as a public water-supply source.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Lo\xc3\xadza Lake is also used for water sports and recreational fishing.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Barrios">Barrios</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Barrios"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/220px-Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/330px-Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png/440px-Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_locator_map.png 2x" data-file-width="847" data-file-height="630" /></a><figcaption>Subdivisions of Trujillo Alto</figcaption></figure>\n<p>Like all municipalities of Puerto Rico, Trujillo Alto is subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Barrios_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Barrios of Puerto Rico">barrios</a>. The municipal buildings, central square and large Catholic church are located in a barrio referred to as <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">"el pueblo"</i></span>.<sup id="cite_ref-Law2015_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law2015-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-map_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-map-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<ol><li><a href="/wiki/Carra%C3%ADzo" title="Carra\xc3\xadzo">Carra\xc3\xadzo</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cuevas,_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Cuevas, Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Cuevas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dos_Bocas,_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Dos Bocas, Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Dos Bocas</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/La_Gloria,_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="La Gloria, Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">La Gloria</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Quebrada_Grande,_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Quebrada Grande, Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Quebrada Grande</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Quebrada_Negrito" title="Quebrada Negrito">Quebrada Negrito</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St._Just,_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="St. Just, Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">St. Just</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Trujillo_Alto_barrio-pueblo" title="Trujillo Alto barrio-pueblo">Trujillo Alto barrio-pueblo</a></li></ol>\n<p>Trujillo Alto\'s townscape is fairly simple. Most of the barrios are spread through the rural section of the city, while the downtown area (Trujillo Alto Pueblo) is small, consisting only of eight primary streets. This gave the city the nickname of the "City of the Eight Streets".<sup id="cite_ref-ed_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ed-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Also, there are no high-rise buildings and structures.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sectors">Sectors</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sectors"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Barrios (which are, in contemporary times, roughly comparable to  <a href="/wiki/Minor_civil_divisions" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor civil divisions">minor civil divisions</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-Barrio-Pueblo_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barrio-Pueblo-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and subbarrios,<sup id="cite_ref-Census_map_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Census_map-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are further subdivided into smaller areas called <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">sectores</i></span>  (<i>sectors</i> in English). The types of <i>sectores</i> may vary, from normally <i>sector</i> to <i>urbanizaci\xc3\xb3n</i> to <i>reparto</i> to <i>barriada</i> to <i>residencial</i>, among others.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Law_1-2001_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Law_1-2001-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Special_Communities">Special Communities</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Special Communities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1236090951">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Office_for_Socioeconomic_and_Community_Development" title="Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development">Puerto Rico Office for Socioeconomic and Community Development</a></div>\n<p><span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Comunidades Especiales de Puerto Rico</i></span> (Special Communities of Puerto Rico) are marginalized communities whose citizens are experiencing a certain amount of <a href="/wiki/Social_exclusion" title="Social exclusion">social exclusion</a>. A map shows these communities occur in nearly every municipality of the commonwealth. Of the 742 places that were on the list in 2014, the following barrios, communities, sectors, or neighborhoods were in Trujillo Alto: San Nicol\xc3\xa1s neighborhood, Bethania, Comunidad Talanco, El Hoyo II, El Resbal\xc3\xb3n, Parcelas Carra\xc3\xadzo, Parcelas Ram\xc3\xb3n T. Col\xc3\xb3n, Sector Arayanes, Sector La Pr\xc3\xa1, Sector Las Cruces, Sector Los Nu\xc3\xb1ez, Villa Escondida, Villa Margarita and Villa Platanal.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordpress.com_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordpress.com-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Climate">Climate</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Climate"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div>\n<table class="wikitable mw-collapsible" style="width:auto; color:#FFFFFF; border-left-width:medium" class="notheme">168.9\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td colspan="14" style="text-align:center;font-size:95%;">Source: <a href="/wiki/NOAA" class="mw-redirect" title="NOAA">NOAA</a><sup id="cite_ref-NOAA_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NCEI_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NCEI-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n</div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Tourism">Tourism</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tourism"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>There are several places of interest for tourists to visit in Trujillo Alto. The <i>Bicentenary Walkway</i>, located in the entrance to the city at the <a href="/wiki/PR-181" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-181">PR-181</a>, features the remodeled historic steel bridge (one of the first permanent crossings of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">Grande de Loiza River</a>) as well as a <a href="/wiki/Gazebo" title="Gazebo">gazebo</a>. It was built in 2001 to commemorate the 200th anniversary of the founding of Trujillo Alto.\n</p><p>Also on the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_181" title="Puerto Rico Highway 181">PR-181</a>, is the <a href="/wiki/Luis_Mu%C3%B1oz_Mar%C3%ADn" title="Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn">Luis Mu\xc3\xb1oz Mar\xc3\xadn Foundation</a> which was established in 1980. It includes a museum, a historic archive, and a park.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Carra%C3%ADzo_Dam" title="Carra\xc3\xadzo Dam">Carra\xc3\xadzo Dam</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Lo%C3%ADza_Lake" title="Lo\xc3\xadza Lake">Lo\xc3\xadza Lake</a> reservoir are also frequently visited. Other places of interest are the <i>Carmelitas de San Jos\xc3\xa9 Convent</i>, the <i>Lourdes Grotto</i>, and the <i>Trujillo Alto Mountain Spring</i>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Economy">Economy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Economy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The economy of Trujillo Alto has relied mostly on agriculture, particularly <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">sugarcane</a>, coffee, tobacco, and minor fruits. <a href="/wiki/Cattle_ranch" class="mw-redirect" title="Cattle ranch">Cattle ranching</a> is also a source of economy in Trujillo Alto. In recent years, commerce and industry have become integral parts of the economy of the city. Trujillo Alto is the site of several factories of nutritional products, wood, metal, electrical machinery, and others. There are also <a href="/wiki/Stone_quarry" class="mw-redirect" title="Stone quarry">stone quarries</a> in town for the production of building materials.\n</p><p>As of 2013, Trujillo Alto\'s unemployment was 10.2%, making it the second municipality with the lowest rate after <a href="/wiki/Guaynabo,_Puerto_Rico" title="Guaynabo, Puerto Rico">Guaynabo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Culture">Culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Festivals_and_events">Festivals and events</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Festivals and events"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Trujillo Alto celebrates its <a href="/wiki/Fiestas_patronales_in_Puerto_Rico" title="Fiestas patronales in Puerto Rico">patron saint</a> festival in September. The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Fiestas Patronales de Santa Cruz</i></span> is a religious and cultural celebration that generally features parades, games, artisans, amusement rides, regional food, and live entertainment.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Festival Trujillano de Orqu\xc3\xaddeas</i></span> (<a href="/wiki/Orchidaceae" class="mw-redirect" title="Orchidaceae">Orchid</a> Festival) has been held in July since 2011. It is an horticultural competition and festival where orchids are ranked, exhibited and sold.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">Festival del Macabeo</i></span> (Macabeo Festival), a festival celebrating a food specific to Trujillo Alto, is celebrated each year around the second week of December.<sup id="cite_ref-Hern\xc3\xa1ndez_2016_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hern\xc3\xa1ndez_2016-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Other festivals and fairs celebrated in Trujillo Alto include an agricultural fair held in January and a <a href="/wiki/Paso_Fino" title="Paso Fino">Paso Fino</a> Festival held in November.\n</p><p>In 2001, Trujillo Alto commemorated its bicentenary with the opening of a new park in the <a href="/wiki/PR-181" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-181">PR-181</a>, which included a remodeling of the historical steel bridge.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Religion">Religion</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Religion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Gruta02.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Gruta02.JPG/220px-Gruta02.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Gruta02.JPG/330px-Gruta02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Gruta02.JPG/440px-Gruta02.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1075" data-file-height="806" /></a><figcaption>Our Lady of Lourdes grotto</figcaption></figure>\n<p>There are a number of churches and chapels from several denominations in Trujillo Alto. The main parish, Santa Cruz Church, was built in 1817. Part of a related structure was damaged by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_San_Felipe_Segundo" class="mw-redirect" title="Hurricane San Felipe Segundo">Hurricane San Felipe</a> in 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-prfogui_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prfogui-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The current structure was designed by Luis Perocier and built in 1933.<sup id="cite_ref-ed_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ed-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>Trujillo Alto has also been a place of pilgrimage for <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholics</a> after a shrine to <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Lourdes" title="Our Lady of Lourdes">Our Lady of Lourdes</a> was blessed in 1925. The site also features a grotto dedicated to Our Lady of Lourdes. The <i>Lourdes grotto</i> is visited frequently by religious people and tourists.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There\'s also a <a href="/wiki/Convent" title="Convent">convent</a> in Trujillo Alto called the <i>Convento Carmelitas de San Jos\xc3\xa9</i>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Sports">Sports</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Sports"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Trujillo Alto doesn\'t have a professional sports team. However, there are several sports facilities in the city for amateur and novice leagues. In 2011, the Rub\xc3\xa9n S\xc3\xa1nchez Monta\xc3\xb1ez Court in Trujillo Alto, hosted the <a href="/wiki/Cangrejeros_de_Santurce_(basketball)" title="Cangrejeros de Santurce (basketball)">Cangrejeros de Santurce</a> team of the <a href="/wiki/Baloncesto_Superior_Nacional" title="Baloncesto Superior Nacional">Baloncesto Superior Nacional</a> (BSN), which is the professional basketball league. The facility has a capacity for 2,250 people.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In September, Trujillo Alto celebrates the <i>Arrecosta\'o</i> Marathon, which is one of the most important events in the city. The race has been celebrated yearly since 1985. It originally covered a 6.2-mile (10-kilometer) trajectory around town, but in 2007, it was shortened to 3.1 miles (5 kilometers).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In 2010, the marathon was recognized as one of the best organized events of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Lo%C3%ADza_Lake" title="Lo\xc3\xadza Lake">Lo\xc3\xadza Lake</a> is also a frequent spot for <a href="/wiki/Sport_fishing" class="mw-redirect" title="Sport fishing">sports</a> and <a href="/wiki/Recreational_fishing" title="Recreational fishing">recreational fishing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The lake features a wide variety of fishes like: <a href="/wiki/Largemouth_bass" title="Largemouth bass">largemouth bass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peacock_bass" title="Peacock bass">peacock bass</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sea_chubs" class="mw-redirect" title="Sea chubs">sea chubs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tilapia" title="Tilapia">tilapia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Beardfish" title="Beardfish">beardfish</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Cuisine">Cuisine</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Cuisine"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <i>macabeo</i> is the most known typical food of Trujillo Alto. It is a <a href="/wiki/Frying" title="Frying">fried</a> dish made with <a href="/wiki/Cooking_banana" title="Cooking banana">plantains</a> and meat.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The popularity of the dish is such that a festival is celebrated annually on its honor. The <i>Macabeo Festival</i> began in the early 1980s and is held annually in December.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Demographics">Demographics</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1224496135">.mw-parser-output .us-census-pop{border-spacing:1px;border:1px solid class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br />1899 (shown as 1900)<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 1910\xe2\x80\x931930<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><br />1930\xe2\x80\x931950<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 1960\xe2\x80\x932000<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 2010<sup id="cite_ref-US2010Census_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-US2010Census-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n2020<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></td></tr>\n</tbody></table>\n<p>The population of Trujillo Alto increased steadily during the 20th century and until the year 2000. There was a 1.2% decrease from 2000 to 2010 and a 9.5% decrease from 2010 to 2020.  According to the 2020 census, the municipality had 67,740 inhabitants. Despite the decline, in 2020 Trujillo Alto was the tenth largest municipality in Puerto Rico, in terms of population.\n</p><p>According to the 2010 Census, 72% of the population identifies themselves as <a href="/wiki/White_Puerto_Ricans" title="White Puerto Ricans">White</a>, and 14.6% as <a href="/wiki/Afro%E2%80%93Puerto_Ricans" title="Afro\xe2\x80\x93Puerto Ricans">African-American</a>. Also, 47.5% of the population identified themselves as males, and 52.5% as females. Finally, 25% of the population is under 18 years old. The next biggest percentage of population (20.7%) is between 35 and 49 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Government">Government</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Government"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico_city_hall.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_city_hall.JPG/250px-Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_city_hall.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_city_hall.JPG/375px-Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_city_hall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_city_hall.JPG/500px-Trujillo_Alto%2C_Puerto_Rico_city_hall.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a><figcaption>Trujillo Alto City Hall</figcaption></figure>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mayoralty_in_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayoralty in Puerto Rico">Mayoralty in Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<p>Like all municipalities in Puerto Rico, Trujillo Alto is administered by a mayor. The first official mayor of Trujillo Alto was Juan Francisco Carazo, who was one of the residents that vouched for the founding of the town in 1801. The mayor as of July 16, 2022 is Pedro Rodr\xc3\xadguez Gonz\xc3\xa1lez.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Before him was <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Cruz_Cruz" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Cruz Cruz">Jos\xc3\xa9 Luis Cruz Cruz</a> (from the <a href="/wiki/Popular_Democratic_Party_of_Puerto_Rico" class="mw-redirect" title="Popular Democratic Party of Puerto Rico">Popular Democratic Party</a>), who was elected in the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rican_general_election,_2004" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rican general election, 2004">2004 general election</a>.\n</p><p>The city belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Senatorial_district_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico Senatorial district VIII">Puerto Rico Senatorial district VIII</a>, which is represented by two Senators. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_A._Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Pedro A. Rodr\xc3\xadguez">Pedro A. Rodr\xc3\xadguez</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luis_Daniel_Rivera" title="Luis Daniel Rivera">Luis Daniel Rivera</a> were elected as District Senators.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Representatives <a href="/wiki/Javier_Aponte_Dalmau" title="Javier Aponte Dalmau">Javier Aponte Dalmau</a> (District 38) and <a href="/wiki/Roberto_Rivera_Ruiz" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberto Rivera Ruiz">Roberto Rivera Ruiz</a> (District 39), both from the PPD, represent different regions of Trujillo Alto in the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_House_of_Representatives" class="mw-redirect" title="Puerto Rico House of Representatives">House of Representatives</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Symbols">Symbols</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Symbols"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The <span title="Spanish-language text"><i lang="es">municipio</i></span> has an official flag and coat of arms.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Flag">Flag</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Flag"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The flag of Trujillo Alto features a white background with the town\'s <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> in the center.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Coat of arms"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>The coat of arms features a shield with a blue border, with eight spurts of water representing the many <a href="/wiki/Spring_(hydrology)" title="Spring (hydrology)">springs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Creek_(stream)" class="mw-redirect" title="Creek (stream)">creeks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">rivers</a> that flow in town. Inside the shield, there\'s a silver field with three green mountains and a blue Latin cross above them. The flag features a white banner below the shield with the name of the city, and a <a href="/wiki/Coronet" title="Coronet">coronet</a> in the form of a five-tower mural crown alluding to the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_crown" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish crown">Spanish crown</a>. The banner and the coronet aren\'t featured in the flag.<sup id="cite_ref-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LexJuris_(Leyes_y_Jurisprudencia)_de_Puerto_Rico_2020-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Nicknames">Nicknames</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Nicknames"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>Trujillo Alto is known by various names. It is known as the "<a href="/wiki/Spring_(hydrology)" title="Spring (hydrology)">City of Springs</a>" for its many rivers and creeks. It is also known as the "<i>Town of the Eight Streets</i>" because the downtown area consists of eight streets. Trujillo Alto is also known as the "<i>City in the Country</i>", for its proximity to the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_Metropolitan_Area" class="mw-redirect" title="San Juan Metropolitan Area">San Juan Metropolitan Area</a> despite being mostly a mountain town.<sup id="cite_ref-ed_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ed-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Finally, it is also called the "<i>Laid-back Town</i>".\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Transportation">Transportation</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Transportation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Historic_Bridge_in_Trujillo_Alto.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Historic_Bridge_in_Trujillo_Alto.JPG/220px-Historic_Bridge_in_Trujillo_Alto.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="329" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Historic_Bridge_in_Trujillo_Alto.JPG/330px-Historic_Bridge_in_Trujillo_Alto.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Historic_Bridge_in_Trujillo_Alto.JPG/440px-Historic_Bridge_in_Trujillo_Alto.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3872" /></a><figcaption>Historic steel bridge in Trujillo Alto on the <a href="/wiki/PR-181" class="mw-redirect" title="PR-181">PR-181</a></figcaption></figure>\n<p>The main road to Trujillo Alto is the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_181" title="Puerto Rico Highway 181">PR-181</a> that crosses the municipality from north to south. Distance from the <a href="/wiki/San_Juan,_Puerto_Rico" title="San Juan, Puerto Rico">capital</a> is 11 miles (18&#160;km), with a travel time of roughly 15 minutes by car.<sup id="cite_ref-psh_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-psh-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other highways that lead to Trujillo Alto are PR-852 of the <a href="/wiki/Quebrada_Grande,_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Quebrada Grande, Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Quebrada Grande</a> neighborhood and <a href="/wiki/Dos_Bocas,_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Dos Bocas, Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Dos Bocas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Highway_175" title="Puerto Rico Highway 175">PR-175</a> of the neighborhood <a href="/wiki/Carra%C3%ADzo" title="Carra\xc3\xadzo">Carra\xc3\xadzo</a>, the Las Cumbres Avenue and PR-851 from <a href="/wiki/La_Gloria,_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="La Gloria, Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">La Gloria</a> neighborhood.\n</p><p>In the past, communication with the town was limited because of its location on the other side of the <a href="/wiki/R%C3%ADo_Grande_de_Lo%C3%ADza" title="R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza">R\xc3\xado Grande de Lo\xc3\xadza</a>. The construction of two bridges in 1826 helped facilitate access to the town. In 1939, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Army" title="United States Army">United States Army</a> built a steel bridge in the entrance to the town on the PR-181, to replace one of the older ones. Although the bridge is no longer used for vehicles, it has become a symbol of the city and still stands today.<sup id="cite_ref-historia_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historia-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>The northern part of Trujillo Alto is serviced by the <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico_Metropolitan_Bus_Authority" title="Puerto Rico Metropolitan Bus Authority">Puerto Rico Metropolitan Bus Authority</a>, with various stops along the PR-181 and nearby neighborhoods.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Other public transportation in the city is provided by taxis and independent public cars.\n</p><p>There are 11 bridges in Trujillo Alto.<sup id="cite_ref-bridge_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bridge-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_natives_and_residents">Notable natives and residents</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Notable natives and residents"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Trujillo_Alto,_Puerto_Rico" title="Category:People from Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico">Category:People from Trujillo Alto, Puerto Rico</a></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dariam_Acevedo" title="Dariam Acevedo">Dariam Acevedo</a> \xe2\x80\x93 1984 Olympic gold medalist representing Puerto Rico in female beach volleyball</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jasmine_Camacho-Quinn" title="Jasmine Camacho-Quinn">Jasmine Camacho-Quinn</a> \xe2\x80\x93 2020 Olympic gold medalist representing Puerto Rico in Women\'s 100m Hurdles, was able to represent Puerto Rico because her family, namely her mother, is from Trujillo Alto.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Tulio_Larr%C3%ADnaga" title="Tulio Larr\xc3\xadnaga">Tulio Larr\xc3\xadnaga</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Architect of the city of San Juan in 1872.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yolandita_Monge" title="Yolandita Monge">Yolandita Monge</a> \xe2\x80\x93 International singer, songwriter, actress, and television personality.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Irad_Ortiz_Jr" class="mw-redirect" title="Irad Ortiz Jr">Irad Ortiz Jr</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Champion jockey and winner of over 3000 races in the USA. Also three-time consecutive winner (2018,2019,2020) of the Eclipse Award for outstanding jockey of the year.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Ortiz_(jockey)" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Ortiz (jockey)">Jose Ortiz</a> \xe2\x80\x93 Champion jockey and winner of over 2300 races in the USA. 2017 winner of the Eclipse Award for outstanding jockey of the year.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2
